<div id="review_185772389" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/185772389" />
    <a title="Jenn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3957464-jenn"><img alt="Jenn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360078699p2/3957464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/185772389?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenn" href="/user/show/3957464-jenn">Jenn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=adult-fiction">adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=3-star-reads">3-star-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=paranormal-supernatural">paranormal-supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=shapeshifting-madness">shapeshifting-madness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer185772389" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10701416594884043737">So I had originally rated this book 4 stars back in 2011. Apparently I'm a more picky reader now lol. <br/><br/>Well, we finally got back to good ole police work with this one. And boy was I happy. Don't get me wrong, these books will always be my guilty pleasures but they've been lacking lately and quite ridiculous. The reason I fell in love with these books was the core characters and the crime factor. Anita had a job, a life - and she was good at it until it all became about sex.<br/><br/>This book starts right </span>
  <span id="freeText10701416594884043737" style="display:none">So I had originally rated this book 4 stars back in 2011. Apparently I'm a more picky reader now lol. <br /><br />Well, we finally got back to good ole police work with this one. And boy was I happy. Don't get me wrong, these books will always be my guilty pleasures but they've been lacking lately and quite ridiculous. The reason I fell in love with these books was the core characters and the crime factor. Anita had a job, a life - and she was good at it until it all became about sex.<br /><br />This book starts right off with Anita doing her marshal duties, which of course means we get more Edward - which I'm always fine with because he has somehow become the best character in this series. Anyway, Anita and Edward solving murders, I'm here for it. We got a few familiar faces, but I'm still missing my core group. The cast has become so big that I forget a lot of these new people right after I meet them. Anyone that's come in after book 12, yeah forget it, I don't remember you. And that's a problem. These new characters aren't fleshed out. They're just sex bait and it's frustrating because not only are you not allowing your characters to mature and grow (mostly because it seems like you forgot about them), but then you're introducing characters for a hot minute that we're suddenly supposed to care about. Well I don't, so you failed.<br /><br />Side note: can Anita just grow up and learn to feed herself like an actual adult? The fact that multiple times every book someone has to remind the girl to eat is ridiculous. And not only that, she pouts about it every time. Even though she knows the outcome, apparently this makes her a strong independent female - no, it just makes you stupid. It seems Anita keeps losing brain cells the more sex she has. What I wouldn't give for her to finally own her sexuality and stop whining every book. <br /><br />Also, Olaf. Why is he still alive? It literally makes no sense. He's creepy and not in a fun way that makes me want to read more about him, no I want him gone. Dead. There's no point to him. <br /><br />I know it seems like I complained a lot about this one, but mostly they are the same complaints I have about the series recently . But the plot here was better and there was less sex, so yay! Progress. I have also finally reached the point where I originally stopped reading the series so everything after this one will be all new to me. Here's hoping they keep getting better, we get our core group back, Anita grows up, and Olaf dies. I know, it's a lot to wish for but a girl can dream, can't she?<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12246178178824189187">Anita Blake has grown to a fully mature woman, finally! <br/><br/>Hit List brings a confident Anita back to her faithful readers who rolled along with her emotional self- discovery and her seemingly endless sexual hang-ups. <br/><br/>I understood in previous novels we were all watching a character develop as if she was a real human being working through major emotional issues and questioning her own morality. Many people have complained she and her paramours are too whiny, too demanding, too… much and I have always</span>
  <span id="freeText12246178178824189187" style="display:none">Anita Blake has grown to a fully mature woman, finally! <br /><br />Hit List brings a confident Anita back to her faithful readers who rolled along with her emotional self- discovery and her seemingly endless sexual hang-ups. <br /><br />I understood in previous novels we were all watching a character develop as if she was a real human being working through major emotional issues and questioning her own morality. Many people have complained she and her paramours are too whiny, too demanding, too… much and I have always held onto the belief that Laurell K. Hamilton was leading us up to something and I believe that we are seeing the fruits of that labor in “Hit List.”<br /><br />“Hit List” gives us a confident Anita, finally being secure in her sexual life and her professional life. Edward is back also (I love his character) and it’s a fully fleshed out story line not just Edward thrown in to the story to sell to his fans, we see via “Hit List” how Edward has changed, if only a little, over the years since he was first introduced.<br />I don’t want to spoil the plot or the characters story for those who have not been able to read it, so I will end with my thoughts that this was one of the best Anita books since “Obsidian Butterfly” and “Narcissus in Chains.” <br />Thank you Laurell for a wonderful read!<br /></span>

<div id="review_206813148" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/206813148" />
    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4254956-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1293752236p2/4254956.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/206813148?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/4254956-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer206813148" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12162805811239925143">I don't know why but this book has been keeping me up at night. Actually, I do know why. Because I can't figure out what happened. I feel like I need to reread the series to dissect when everything went horribly wrong. It has been many years so I can't pinpoint the exact book, but I'm sure many readers could spout it off the top of their heads.<br/><br/>I have one theory that has to do with something major happening in the life of the author. It seems as if Anita changed so dramatically and against charac</span>
  <span id="freeText12162805811239925143" style="display:none">I don't know why but this book has been keeping me up at night. Actually, I do know why. Because I can't figure out what happened. I feel like I need to reread the series to dissect when everything went horribly wrong. It has been many years so I can't pinpoint the exact book, but I'm sure many readers could spout it off the top of their heads.<br /><br />I have one theory that has to do with something major happening in the life of the author. It seems as if Anita changed so dramatically and against character. I feel like the author is writing more about herself and less about the character. Now, I realize that all authors put something of themselves into characters, but this seems over the top. For example, Anita's defensiveness about being a women, short, attractive, having lots of boyfriends, etc. Anita was always a bit insecure so I find it hard to believe that she would all of sudden become the type of woman who thinks everybody is envious of her life or judging her for that lifestyle. Everybody changes and all series show the main character evolving or growing, so I expect Anita to change. However, I would expect her personality to remain the same or become more mature as she herself aged. This doesn't seem the case. In fact, I feel the opposite that Anita became stupid and immature.<br /><br />Several readers express feelings that the series took a turn for the worse when the sex scenes started getting more and more prevalent and graphic. I don't really think this is what put most people off. It was the story line and Anita. She went from being this badass warrior and a bit of a prude (remember her telling Richard she wouldn't sleep with anyone until marriage) to being a nursemaid and a porn star. In this book she wants to go hold hands with the marshall in the hospital whose having a hard time dealing with becoming a shifter instead of catch the bad guys. What?? She treated Jean-Claude like crap for forever and now she wants tons of men to follow her around. Did one of her lovers literally **** her brains out? Maybe she has multiple personality disorder? Or...she really died in Guilty Pleasures and we are going to discover that Anita's heaven is tons of sex with really hot guys while occasionly hunting bad guys? <br /><br />There are so many questions I have about this series. What I really want to know is why the stories have gotten so boring? I felt like I was missing something about the story. We were dropped in the middle of it and lots of interesting things happened before we got there. I feel like the books used to be much longer and more involved. I don't think I can solve the mystery anytime soon but I will go back and try to find the characters how they used to be. Oh, how I miss The Killing Dance. I really only wanted Anita to be with Jean-Claude any way. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12162805811239925143" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_174530800" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/174530800" />
    <a title="Dianne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1401819-dianne"><img alt="Dianne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604666390p2/1401819.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/174530800?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dianne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dianne" href="/user/show/1401819-dianne">Dianne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer174530800" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13730442462270244496">Hit List by Laurell K Hamilton<br/><br/> Is this series nearly over after 20 books or will Ms. Hamilton keep trying to push for more? It seems to me that Ms. Hamilton may be getting somewhat tired of Anita and her Harem and it shows in the writing of this novel. In addition, if Laurell is tired at this point can you imagine just how her longtime fans feel? Luckily, this book is not as horrid as some of her previous attempts at writing action/erotica. It goes a long way in making up for the previous books </span>
  <span id="freeText13730442462270244496" style="display:none">Hit List by Laurell K Hamilton<br /><br /> Is this series nearly over after 20 books or will Ms. Hamilton keep trying to push for more? It seems to me that Ms. Hamilton may be getting somewhat tired of Anita and her Harem and it shows in the writing of this novel. In addition, if Laurell is tired at this point can you imagine just how her longtime fans feel? Luckily, this book is not as horrid as some of her previous attempts at writing action/erotica. It goes a long way in making up for the previous books that have so insulted her fans' intelligence and hopefully Ms. Hamilton may have finally given up on the assumption that we (her long-time fans) will stick with the series no matter how faulty the writing.<br /> One of the biggest problems in this book is that there is a lot of repetition both in dialogue and in character types. Some dialogue and descriptions seem to be reproduced nearly word for word in the space of two chapters. It is as if Ms. Hamilton is too tired to think of anything new to throw at Anita and Crew. Perhaps her beta readers and editor fell down on their jobs. Marshal Raborn seems to be a caricature or a regurgitation of Dolph. Dolph when he was at his worst. Remember the books in which he is angry and takes it out on Anita? I’m tired of these kinds of repetitive ‘macho’ men and Anita having to defend herself; as if Ms. Hamilton really needs to remind us that Anita is MORE than just a sex object now. Oh, wait…maybe she does?<br />One good thing about this book is that the excessive descriptions of long hair are missing since none of her “sweeties” is in it, but we do get descriptions of ‘anime’ hair. Also missing are the ramblings of Anita discussing her wardrobe and the ever-popular lengthy dialogues and soliloquies just before she deigns to have sex with anyone. Amazingly, sex takes a backseat to the other goings-on in this book. No sex until halfway through the book!!!<br />But Anita’s nearly constant need to size herself up against all the other women, to constantly be reminding us of how cute, curvy and large breasted she is, how desirable she is, is taking a major toll on this reader. It’s annoying and makes me wonder just how insecure the author is in her own life. <br /><br />Now for the ending and my thoughts-------------SPOILERS---------SPOILERS--------SPOILERS<br /><br /> So we have a conclusion to the Mother of All Darkness, but did we have an ending? Is this a true death of Marmee? On the other hand, will this be a red herring? Why did Ms. Hamilton choose to end the “Big Bad” but not the series? I’m annoyed that we’ve gone through twenty books with perhaps ten of them building up to this and then it is such a letdown. Although I do find it interesting that Olof/Otto is now going to be a lion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13730442462270244496" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_176123660" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/176123660" />
    <a title="Cat Russell  (Addicted2Heroines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4250664-cat-russell-addicted2heroines"><img alt="Cat Russell  (Addicted2Heroines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1405087473p2/4250664.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/176123660?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cat Russell  (Addicted2Heroines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cat Russell  (Addicted2Heroines)" href="/user/show/4250664-cat-russell-addicted2heroines">Cat Russell  (Addicted2Heroines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780143145639" href="/book/show/9400850-hit-list">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4250664-cat-russell-addicted2heroines?shelf=highly-recommend">highly-recommend</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer176123660" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9570573838596851365"><i>"Lately, I didn't have to disassociate to pull the trigger. That probably should have worried me, but it didn't. Olaf worried me. One monster at a time, even if one of them is yourself."</i><br/> <br/><br/><br/>I enjoyed the change in Edward and Anita's relationship. He's finally admitting that he cares for her and wants to keep her safe. Edward's character has been one of my favorites ever since I started this series, so I was glad to see that he played a larger role in this story. <br/><br/>I'm not afraid to admit that I love </span>
  <span id="freeText9570573838596851365" style="display:none"><i>"Lately, I didn't have to disassociate to pull the trigger. That probably should have worried me, but it didn't. Olaf worried me. One monster at a time, even if one of them is yourself."</i><br /> <br /><br /><br />I enjoyed the change in Edward and Anita's relationship. He's finally admitting that he cares for her and wants to keep her safe. Edward's character has been one of my favorites ever since I started this series, so I was glad to see that he played a larger role in this story. <br /><br />I'm not afraid to admit that I love Olaf and all of his homicidal creepiness. He has an interesting twist at the end and I can't wait to see how it plays out in future stories.<br /><br />I loved the action but I still didn't feel like it was enough. The ending felt too rushed especially since what occured was something that has been building up for a long time now.<br /><br />There were only two significant problems that I had with this story. The first was that Anita's thoughts and responses have become entirely too predictable. I knew what she would say or what her thoughts would be to most situations before I read them. I can't decide if it's a lack of creativity in the writing or if it's because we know her so well after reading 20 of her books. Even so, it has a tendency to make most conversations rather dull.<br /><br />I also had a problem with characters constantly asking "What?" or "What does that mean?" in nearly every conversation. I suppose that's the author's way of feeding information to the reader, but it wasn't always necessary. Sometimes they were asking "What does that mean?" even when Anita's meaning seemed obvious. I've also noticed this happens a lot in her Meredith Gentry series as well.<br /><br />Overall I enjoyed it but I couldn't help but wonder what Jean-Claude, Nathaniel, and Micah were up to back at home. I suppose I will just have to keep wondering because I'm sure it will be a long, long wait before we find out. </span>

How many mutha-cluckers do you have to freak before it becomes inexcusable. <br /><br />Anita is now the definition of a prostitute. She gives her body (sex) to collect the necessary animals or whatnot to keep herself and the triumvirate powerful (benefit). The whole click must give up the dick and contribute when needed.<br /><br />I am still hoping that Asher finds his way as Hamilton has made him into a whiny-baby-bitch. <br /><br />The men seem to be a bunch of bitch-asses bowing down to Anita. I'm all for female power, but this is ridic. <br /><br />Why am I still reading then, you ask. My answer: Hope. Hope for that one moment Jean-Claude gets what he wants. Hope that I'll get a story that is mostly un-sexual. Hope that Anita sets her minions free to live their lives. Hope for a traditional LK read.<br /><br />I will never buy another one of her books unless she reverts to her origins though. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15787275153510782854" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_182727982" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/182727982" />
    <a title="Karina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3685170-karina"><img alt="Karina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1428689137p2/3685170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/182727982?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karina" href="/user/show/3685170-karina">Karina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3685170-karina?shelf=lkh_anita-blake">lkh_anita-blake</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer182727982" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15003720378246015576">DON'T WASTE YOUR MONEY! This one was really disappointing. I read Bullet and Hit List back to back, and the two don't make any sense at all together. Its clear that Hamilton was writing one story, decided midway to break it into two then couldn't figure out how to make them work so she threw a bunch of nonsensical subplots into the mix (trying to increase page count no doubt) and now neither story makes any sense at all. So frustrating!<br/><br/>Hit List drags along with very little of any consequence hap</span>
  <span id="freeText15003720378246015576" style="display:none">DON'T WASTE YOUR MONEY! This one was really disappointing. I read Bullet and Hit List back to back, and the two don't make any sense at all together. Its clear that Hamilton was writing one story, decided midway to break it into two then couldn't figure out how to make them work so she threw a bunch of nonsensical subplots into the mix (trying to increase page count no doubt) and now neither story makes any sense at all. So frustrating!<br /><br />Hit List drags along with very little of any consequence happening for 90% of the book. LKH pulls out her tired standbys/stereotypes to drag out the page count. Why is it that in every single case that Anita works, there is some chauvinist cop who is so judgmental of Anita's love life that he is willing to risk his career to show her up? Why is it that every single person Anita comes into contact with either despises her for no apparent reason or is so completely enthralled with her that they can't resist her? Anita started out as a slightly insecure badass warrior, now she's somehow become a narcissistic nymphomaniac pansy who can only defeat her enemies through the power of her magic vagina! <br /><br />Oh, and guess what - Anita adds yet another male to her harem (because she is completely irresistible, and god-forbid she have a one night stand!). Seriously? This author loves to go on and on about female empowerment and sexual freedom, but she won't let her main characters have any freedom at all - they're all just shackled to one another in an plural marriage that is constantly increasing in size. With this number of partners, no one can possibly be happy because it simply isn't possible for anyone's physical or emotional needs to be met. I could care less if Anita has sex with multiple partners - but she does't need to bring every single one of them home! How are we, as readers, supposed to keep up? <br /><br />Finally, about 90% through the book, we reach the conclusion that has been building for the past eleven books...and it's all wrapped up neatly and easily in about two paragraphs. What a let down. Most of what was built up in Bullet, wasn't even used or needed for the conclusion in Hit List. The book concludes with a tiny (3 page) epilogue in which LKH quickly wraps up the entire situation - without actually explaining any of it. Its like, she reached her minimum page count and decided she was done. Lazy and pathetic!<br /><br />I want to give up on this series, I really do, but I've stuck it out for twenty freaking books now - I'm invested and its driving me crazy. I can say this though, don't waste your money - this one can definitely wait until its in paperback or better yet, wait until its available for free at the library.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15003720378246015576" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_176323487" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/176323487" />
    <a title="Bethany" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2234912-bethany"><img alt="Bethany" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407561756p2/2234912.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/176323487?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bethany" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bethany" href="/user/show/2234912-bethany">Bethany</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer176323487" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9217488341787011540">Was really really disappointed by the ending. It was so anti-climactic and then i was left with a summary of what was happening with a few characters that were't even on stage in the book. The rest of the book was another version of scenes that have been in so many other books, such as, the cop doesn't like Anita because she's a woman. Anita is better than everybody and Edward likes her more. Oh no, i didn't eat so i have to feed the ardeur. I was hoping for more plot and story line than I got. </span>
  <span id="freeText9217488341787011540" style="display:none">Was really really disappointed by the ending. It was so anti-climactic and then i was left with a summary of what was happening with a few characters that were't even on stage in the book. The rest of the book was another version of scenes that have been in so many other books, such as, the cop doesn't like Anita because she's a woman. Anita is better than everybody and Edward likes her more. Oh no, i didn't eat so i have to feed the ardeur. I was hoping for more plot and story line than I got. It seemed like LKH wanted to get rid of the big bad monster and move onto other things, but that part of the story was so anti-climactic that I found myself thinking really? this is it? <br /><br />I've also thought and LKH has said, that Anita is a fictional version of herself. It seems that now that things are going better for LKH in her own life, she wants Anita to be the same way, but Anita's world is too messy and complicated to be able to do that. A review I read after Bullet came out suggested that even though she's come to terms with her powers, she has so many ties to so many people that it's hard to keep track of everybody. This reviewer suggested that Mommy Darkest somehow strip Anita of all of her metaphysical ties and then see how she still felt about the men and people in her life. at first i was appalled, but that is almost what this series needs. If she can beat the biggest bad without much of a fight then where is this series going to go from here? <br /><br />Anita keeps saying that she's tired of the crime scenes and just wants to be at home with her sweeties. Well, it seems that LKH has lost her passion to write conflict and have bad things happen to her main character to make her stronger. Its like she adds some things to put something into a book, but nothing really bad ever happens. Anita has become so powerful that she just walks over everybody. This series is flagging and there's no end in sight. I respect authors who can say, this is the end of the story arch. LKH might need to think about that with this series or go back to the roots and figure out how to get out of this mess of characters that you can't keep track of or get close to and write a book that's more about plot than feelings.<br /><br />Do i recommend this book to others? not any more than i've recommended the last ones. I say to new readers, books 1-9 are great but once the obsession with sex and being a woman who is better than me starts, it's not nearly as entertaining.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9217488341787011540" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+1K0JN1IZaM1B60nfnSroHN7v03l4grWPGOaOqky4apKbG4LiD1V1UEOnS4kEAwmC941KZZYXzzg9TpsK5OPIw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer18361270348314616498">Laurell K. Hamilton is one of the leading writers of paranormal fiction. A #1 New York Times bestselling author, Hamilton writes the popular Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter novels and the Meredith Gentry series. She is also the creator of a bestselling comic book series based on her Anita Blake novels and published by Marvel Comics. Hamilton is a full-time writer and lives in the suburbs of St. Louis </span>
  <span id="freeText18361270348314616498" style="display:none">Laurell K. Hamilton is one of the leading writers of paranormal fiction. A #1 New York Times bestselling author, Hamilton writes the popular Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter novels and the Meredith Gentry series. She is also the creator of a bestselling comic book series based on her Anita Blake novels and published by Marvel Comics. Hamilton is a full-time writer and lives in the suburbs of St. Louis with her family.</span>
